7. Let f(x) be a complete polynomial, with real coefficients and v, v' are 
respectively the number of variations and continuations of signs in the 
sequence of its coefficients. If all roots of / ( x) = 0 are real prove that 
the equation has v positive roots and v' negative roots. 
[A polynomial aoxn + a 1xn-l + • • • + an is said to be a complete 
polynomial if no ai is zero.] 
_Since / ( x) is a complete polynomial, if two consecutive elements in 
the sequence of coefficients of f ( x) show a variation of signs then the two 
corresponding elements in the sequence of coefficients of f(-x) show a 
continuation of signs and vice-versa. 
Therefore v' is the number of variations of signs in the sequence of 
coefficients of f(-x). 
Since f(x) is a complete polynomial, O is. not a root of f(x) = O. By 
deduction 3 of the rule, the desired result is derived. 
5.3.5. Sturm's method for location of roots. 
Descartes' rule of signs does not give the exact number of real roots 
of an equation. Sturm's method which will be discussed here gives the 
exact number as well as the position of the real roots of an equation with 
real coefficients. 
I 
l,. 

THEORY OF EQUATIONS 
217 
storm's ~unctions .. Le~ f(x) be a polynomial with real coefficients and 
Ji (x) be its first derivative. L~t the operation of finding the h.c.f. of 
f ( x) and /1 ( x) be performed with the following modification. 
"The sign of each :emainder is to be changed before it is used as the 
next divisor and the sign of the last remainder is also to be changed." 
The modified remainders (i.e., the remainders with their signs 
changed) are denoted by /2(x), f 3(x), . . . , fr(x). 
J(x),f1(x), ... ,fr(x) 
are 
called 
Sturm's 
functions 
and 
Ji(x), f2(x), ... , fr(x) are called auxiliary functions. 
In the usual process of finding the h.c.f. of two polynomials we can 
multiply ( or divide) any remainder by a constant, positive or negative 
but in this modified process of forming Strum's auxiliary functions it is 
essential that such multipliers should be positive. 
If q1 ( x), q2 ( x), ... , Qr- 1 ( x) be the quotients in the successive steps, 
the Sturm's functions f, /1, /2, ... , fr are connected by the equations

f(x) has no multiple root. But if f(x) has multiple roots then the h.c.f. 
of f(x) and f 1(x) is a polynomial, say p(x). In this case all the Sturm's 
functions are divisible by p(x) and the remainder - fr(x) = p(x)</>r(x), 
where c/>r(x) is a constant. 
We state below without proof Sturm's theorem for locating the posi-
tion of real roots of an equation. 
Sturm's theorem. 
I. All roots unequal. 
Let f(x) be a polynomial with real coefficients an~ a, bare real n~-
hers ( a < b). The number of real roots of the equation f ( x) = 0 lying 
?etween a and b is equal to the excess of the number of changes of signs 
lil the sequence of Sturm's functions f(x), f1(x), · · ·, fr(x) when x = a 
over the number of changes of signs in the sequence when x = b.

Remarks. The calculation of Sturm's functions becomes very often 
laborious. But labour may be saved by the following considerations. 
1. If there is no multiple root the last function Ir ( x) is a constant and 
its sign only is required. Let a be a root of l r-i(x) = 0 then lr-2(a) 
and fr(a) are of opposite signs, since fr-2(a) = Qr-llr-i(a) - lr(a). 
Therefore the sign of Ir ( x) can be ascertained from the calculation of 
fr-2(0:). Thus the labour of actual calculation of the constant lr(x) can 
be saved. 
2. If at any stage we obtain a function Is ( x) such that all of its roots are 
complex, then the h.c.f. process need not be continued further and the 
determination and location of real roots will be possible from the set of 
functions l(x), l 1(x), ... , f 8 (x), because ls(x) retains the same sign for 
all values of x and no alteration in the number of changes of sign can 
take place in the sequence of functions beyond Is ( x). 
Condition that all roots may be real and distinct. 
Let l(x) be a polynomial of degree n with leading coefficient positive. 
In order to ensure the existence of n distinct real roots, n changes of signs 
must be lost in the sequence of Sturm's functions as x changes from -oo 
to oo. Therefore n + 1 functions must be present in the sequence and the 
leading coefficients of all these functions must be positive.

12. Find the condition that the roots of the equation x3 + 3H x + G == 0 
may have three real and distinct roots.

f(x) = x3 + 3Hx + G, 
f1(x) = x2 + H,

f3(x) = -(G2 + 4H3).

(i) 
there sould be four Sturm's functions and 
' 
(ii) the leading coefficient of each function should be positive.

i.e., H < 0 and G2 +4H3 < o. 
;hese two conditions can be expressed as the single condition 02 -r 
4H < 0, because the condition G2 + 4H3 < 0 implies H < O.

5.5. Symmetric functions of roots. 
A function f of two or more variables is said to be a symmetric func-
tion if f remains unaltered by an interchange of any two of its variables. 
For example, J(x, y, z) = x2y2 + y2 z2 + z2x2 is a symmetric function 
of x, y, z. J(x, y, z) = xy + yz is not symmetric in x, y, z, because f does 
not remain unaltered if x and y are interchanged. 
A symmetric function of the roots of an equation is an expression 
that involves all the roots alike and the expression remains unaltered if 
any two of the roots be interchanged. 
For example, if o:, /3,, be the roots of a cubic equation, o:2 + {32 + 1
2 
is a symmetric function of the roots, while 0:2/3 + 132"/ + ,20 is not a 
symmetric function.

5.6. Transformation of equations. 
When an equation is given it is possible, without knowing its indi-
vidual roots, to obtain a new equation whos_e roots are connected With 
those of the equation by some assigned relation. The meth0d of finding 
the new equation is said to be a trans/ ormation. Such a tr~nsformation 
sometimes helps us to study the nature of the roots of the given equation 
which would have been otherwise a difficult job. 
We will discuss some typical transformation and then take up the 
general problem. 
5.6.1. To transform an equation whose roots are 01, 02, • ••,an into 
another whose roots are ma1, ma2, ... , man. 
Let the equation whose roots are 01, 02, . . . , On be 
Xn + P1Xn-l + P2Xn-2 + · · · + Pn = 0. 
Let y = ma1. 
Then 01 = y/m. 
Since a 1 is a root of the given equation, 
01 n + P10'.1 n-l + P20'.1n-2 + · · · + Pn = 0. 
Therefore (-;i)n + P1(-;i)n-l + P2(-;i)n-2 + · · · + Pn = 0 
or, yn + P1myn-l + p2m2yn-2 + .. . + Pnmn = 0. 
(A) 
This is the transformed equation. 
[Explanation. ma1 is obviously a root of the equation (A). We would 
obtain the same equation (A) if we put y = mai, where ai is any root of 
the given equation. This proves that ma1, ma2, . .. , man are the roots 
of the equation (A). Since the equation (A) is of degree n, the roots 
ma1, ma2, ... , man are the only roots of it.] 
Note 1. We observe that the successive coefficients of the transformed 
equation are obtained by multiplying the successive coefficients of the 
given equation, beginning from the 1st, by 1, m, m 2, . . . , m n respectively. 
Corollary. The transformed equation whose roots are -a1, -a2, · · · 
-an is obtained by changing the signs of the coefficients beginning fro11l 
the second, alternately. 
Note 2. The transformation is useful for the purpose of removing frac-
tional coefficients of an equation or reducing the leading coefficient of 311 
equation to unity. We are to choose a suitable multiplier of the roots 50 
that the transformed equation will have all integral coefficients with the 
leading coefficient unity.

2. One root of the equation 32x3 -14x + 3 = 0 is double another. Solve 
the equation. 
The equation whose roots are double those of the given equation is 
32x3 - 56x + 24 = 0 or, 4x3 - 7 x + 3 = 0. 
Hence the equations 32x3 - 14x + 3 = 0 and 4x3 - 7x + 3 = 0 have a 
common root. 
The h.c.f. of 32x3 - 14x + 3 and 4x3 - 7x + 3 is 2x - 1. 
Therefore ½ and ¼ are roots of the given equation. The other root is 
-}. Hence the roots of the given equation are ½, ¼, -£. 
5.6.2. To transform an equation into one whose roots are reciprocal of 
the roots of a given equation. 
Let the given equation be aoxn+a1xn-1+a2xn-2+- · ·+an-1x+an = 0 
and let the roots be 01, 02, ... , On. 
It is assumed that none of the roots is zero. 
Let y = (l/01). 
Then 01 = (1/y). 
Sincea1 is a root, aoo1n+a101n-1+a201n-2 + • · •+an-101 +an= 0. 
Therefore ao(½)n + a1(½)n-l + a2(¼)n-2 + · · · + an-1(¼) +an= 0 
or, anyn + an-lYn-1 + ... + a1y + ao = 0. 
This is the transformed equation. 
~ote. The coefficients of the given equation appear in the reverse order 
lil the transformed equation.

5.6.3. Let a 1 , a 2 , ... , an be the roots of the equation 
f(x) = aoXn + a1Xn + X1Xn-l +···+an= 0. 
To find the equation whose roots are a1 - h, a2 - h, · · · , 0 n - h, where h 
is a constant. 
Let y = a 1 - h. Then a1 = y + h. 
Since a1 is a root, aoa1 n + a1a1 n-l +·· · +an = 0. 
or, ao(Y + h)n + a1 (y + h)n-l +···+an = 0. 
This can be expressed as Aoxn + A1xn-l + · ··+An= 0, where An is 
the remainder when f ( x) is divided by x - h and let q1 ( x) be the quotient; 
An-l is the remainder when the quotient q1 ( x) is divided by x - h and 
let q2(x) be the quotient. 
Repeating the same process, An-2, An-3, . .. , A1 are obtained as the 
successive remainders and finally Ao = ao. 
Note. Here the transformation that is applied to the equation is given 
by X = y+ h.

n 1 
Therefore (ao, a1, •••,an) = k(an, an-1, ... , a0 ) for some k -::f:. o. 
That is, ao = kan, a1 = kan-l, a2 = kan-2 , ••. , an= kao. 
a0 = kan and an = kao give k = ±1. 
Two cases arise. 
Case I. k = 1. 
In this case ao = an, a1 = an-l, ... , an = ao. 
The coefficients of equidistant terms from the beginning and the end 
are equal in magnitude and have the same sign. The equation is said to 
be a reciprocal equation of the first type ( or first class). 
Case II. k - 1. 
In this case a0 = -an, a 1 = -an-l, ... , an= - ao. 
The coefficients of equidistant terms from the beginning and the end 
are equal in magnitude but of opposite signs. The equation is said to be 
a reciprocal equation of the second type ( or second class)• 
Examples. 
1. The equation x2 + 1 = o is a reciprocal equation of degree 2 and of 
the first type. 
2. The equation 3x3 _ 13x2 + l3x _ 3 = o is a reciprocal equation of 
degree 4 and of the second type. 
3. The equation 2x4 - 5x3 + 5x - 2 = 0 is a reciprocal equation of degree 
4 au<l of the second type. 
4. The equation x4 - x3 - x + 1 = 0 is a reciprocal equation of degree 4 
and of th e first type.

Theorem 5.7.1. If J(x) = O be a reciprocal equation of degree n and 
of the first type then f(x) = xn !(¾)-
Conversely, if f(x) be a polynomial of degree n and f(x) = xnf(¾) then 
f ( x) = 0 is a reciprocal equation of the first type.

= ao + a1 x + · · · + anxn.

This shows that f ( x) = 0 is a reciprocal equation of the first type. 
This completes the proof.

5.11.2. The general solution of a cubic. Cardan's method. 
Let the cubic equation be 
ax3 + 3bx2 + 3cx + d = 0 
(i)

where z = ax+ b, H = ac - b2 , G = a2d - 3abc + 2b3 •

or, z3 - 3uvz - (u3 + v3 ) = 0.

uv=-H u3 +v3 =-G.

5.12.1. Ferrai's solution of a biquadratic equation. 
Ferrari's method reduces the problem of solving a biquadratic 
·

Th' . d 
equa,. 
tion to that of solving two quadratic equations. 
is 18 one by expressin

g 
Let the equation be ax4 + 4bx3 + 6cx2 + 4dx + e = 0. 
Multiplying by a, a2x4 + 4abx3 + 6acx
2 + 4adx + ae = 0 
. . . 
(i) 
Let the left hand expression be expressed as the difference of two 
squares in the form 
(ax2 + 2bx + ).)2 - (mx + n)2. 
Comparing with the left hand expression of (i) we have 
6ac = 4b2 + 2).a- m2 , 
4ad = 4b). - 2mn, 
ae = ).2 - n 2 • 
Eliminating m, n from these we have 
4(b). - ad)2 = (2).a + 4b2 - 6ac)().2 - ae). 
This is a cubic equation in )., giving at least one real root ).1. 
Corresponding to ). = Ai, we have the values of m2 and n2 and 
morever the relation mn = 2bAi - 2ad determines only one value of n 
corresponding to one value of m. 
Thus the given equation is now put in the form 
(ax2 + 2bx + Ai)2 - (mix+ ni)2 = 0, where mi, ni are the values of 
m, n corresponding to Ai. 
The roots of the quadratic equations ax2 + 2bx +Ai± (mix+ ni) = 0 
give the solution of the given biquadratic equation.

5.12.3. Descartes' method of solution of a biquadratic equation. 
Let the biquadratic equation be taken in the standard form 
x4 + 6Hx2 + 4Gx + (ao2 I - 3H2 ) = 0 
(i) 
To solve the equation, let us express the left hand expression as the 
product of two factors in the form 
(x2 + lx + m)(x2 - lx + n). 
Comparing with the left hand expression of (i) we have 
m + n - l2 = 6H 
or, 
m + n 
6H + l2

mn = (a5I - 3H2 ) 
(iv)

(6H + l2) 2 -
1~f
2 = 4(a02 - 3H2 ) 
(v) 
This is a cubic equation in l2 giving l. Then m and n can be deter-
mined and finally the solution of the equation (i) is obtained. 
Note. Unless the cubic equation (v) has rational roots, the numerical 
work for finding the roots of the equation (i) becomes laborious.

6.1, Introduction. 
Let u1 +u2+· · •+un +···be a series where Un is some function of the

is said to be the sequence of partial sums of the series. If the sequence 
{sn} converges to a finite limit s then the series u1 + u2 + ... +Un+ ... 
is said to be convergent and in that cases is said to be the sum of the 
series. If the sequence {Sn} is divergent, the series is said to be divergent. 
We shall discuss in this chapter some methods of finding the sum Sn 
for the series u1 + u2 + · · · + Un + · · ·

6.3. Difference operator A. 
Let us consider a sequence ( u1, u2, ... Un, . . . . .. ) where Un is a func-
tion of positive integral variable n. 
We define Aun= Un+l -
Un. 
Then Au1 = u2 - u1, Au2 = u3 - u2, Au3 = u 4 -
u 3, • • · · · · 
The sequence (Au1, Au2, ... Aun, ... ... ) is said to be the first order 
of differences of the sequence { un}, 

SUMMATION OF SERIES 
291 
We define A2un = A(Aun) = A(un+l - Un). 
The sequence (A2u1, A2u2, A2u3 , .•.•• • ) is said to be the second 
order of differences of the sequence (un). 
In a similar manner the pth order of differences APun where pis a 
positive integer, can be defined for the sequence (un), 
It follows immediately that 
(i) if Un = k, a constant for all n then Aun = 0 for all n, and con-
versely; 
(ii) If (Un) be a sequence in an arithmetic progression having the com-
mon difference d then A Un = constant = d for all n and conversely. 
(iii) If { un} be a sequence in a geometric progression having the com-
mon ratio r then the sequence ( A Un) is also in geometric progression of 
common ratio r.

6.4. Recurring series. 
The series u0 + u1 + u2 + • • • • • • is said to be a recurring series of 
order r if any r + 1 successive terms of the series are connected by the 
relation 
Un + Pl Un-1 + P2Un-2 + · · · + PrUn-r = 0, n > r •·· (i) 
where p1,p2 , .•. ,Pr are constants. The relation (i) is said to be the scale 
of relation of the recurring series. 
Examples. 
1. The series 1 + 2 + 3 + 5 + 8 + 13 + • • • • • • is a recurring series whose 
scale of relation is Un -
Un-1 -
Un-2 = 0, n > 2. The order of the 
recurring series is 2. 
2. The series 1 + 4 + 9 + 16 + 25 + 36 + · · • • • • is a recurring series whose 
scale of relation is Un - 3un-1 + 3un-2 -
Un_3 = 0. The order of the 
recurring seties is 3. 
The series uo + u1x + u2x2 + · · · · · · is said to be a recurring series 
of order r if any r + 1 successive coefficients of the series are connected 
by the relation 
Un+ Pl Un-1 + P2Un-2 + · · · + PrUn-r = 0, n > r ... (ii) 
where p1,P2, ... ,Pr are constants. The relation (ii) is said to be the 
scale of relation of the recurring series. 
Some authors define the scale of relation in a different way. 
The series uo + u1x + u2x2 + · · · · · • is said to be a recurring series 
of order r if any r + 1 successive terms of the series are connected by 
the relation

We shall accept either of these definitions.

beginning of a recurring series be known then the whole series can be 
constructed. 
For example, if uo = l, U1 = 3 and Un -

recurring series be given then the scale of relation can be determined.

6.5. C + iS method of summation. 
We now discuss a method of finding the sum of two real series 
ao + a1 cos 0 + a2 cos 20 + · .. · · · (i) 
a1 sin0 + a2 sin 20 + · · · · · · (ii) 
where 0 is real and a0 , a1, a2, • • • are constants. 
Let the complex series 
ao + a1eiO + a2e2iO + ...... (iii) 
be convergent for some 0 and f ( 0) be the sum. Let f ( 0) be expressed 
as A + iB where A, B are real. Then 
A+ iB = a0 + a1(cos0 + isin0) + a2(cos20 + isin20) + · · · 
This implies the convergence of the series (i) and (ii) and 
A = ao + a1 cos 0 + a2 cos 20 + · · · · · · 
B = a1 sin 0 + a2 sin 20 + · · · · · · 
Therefore in order to find the sum of either of the series (i) and 
(ii) we try to find the sum of the complex series (iii) in its region of 
convergence and then express the sum f(0) in the form C + iS where 
C and S are real. 
The sums of the series ( i) and (ii) for the corresponding 0 are given 
by C and S respectively.

7.1. Continued fraction. 
An expression of the form 
a+ 
b2 
1 
a2+ 63 
a3+··· 
where a's and b's are all integers with bi =I 
i > 1, a1 > 0, is called a continued fraction. 
The continued fraction is also denoted by 
0 for i > 2, ai > 0 for 
a1 +_h_J?.a_ · · • 
a2+ a3+ 
a1, t, ! , · · · are called elements of the continued fraction. 
If the number of elements be finite, the continued fraction is said to 
be a finite continued fraction. 
If the number of elements be infinite, the continued fraction is said 
to be an infinite continued fraction. 
The value of the fraction obtained by stopping at some stage is called 
a convergent of the continued fraction. 
For the continued fraction a1 + b2+ b3+ ... 
a2 
a3 
the first convergent = a1, 
the second convergent = a1 + b., 
a2 
the third convergent = a1 + b2+ h, 
a2 
a3 
As the number of convergents is finite in a finite continued fraction, 
the value qf the last convergent gives the value of a finite continued 
fraction. 
In an infinite continued fraction, the number of convergents is clearly 
infinite. If u1 , u2 , u3 , • • • be the successive convergents of the continued 
fraction, the continued fraction is said to be convergent if the sequence 
{un} be convergent. In this case lim Un is said to be the value of the 
continued fraction. 
If however the sequence {un} be not convergent, the continued frac-
t' 
. 
' 
ion is said to be divergent. 
For example, the continued fraction 1 + 2~ 2~ • • • is convergent, but 
the continued fraction ...L .=! - 1 ... is divergent.

If a simple continued fraction be finite then there is a finite number 
of quotients and the last convergent gives the value of the continued 
fraction. 
Since each convergent Un is of the form ~ where Pn, qn are positive 
integers, each convergent is a rational number and therefore the value of 
a finite simple continued fraction is a positive rational number. 
We now show that every positive rational number can be expressed 
as a finite simple continued fraction.

1,4. Integral solution of the equation ax + by = c. 
In Theorem 3.2.15 we have seen that the equation ax+ by= c where 
a b, care integers and (a, b) /= (0, 0), has an integral solution if and only 
if gcd( a, b) is a divisor of c. 
.

prime to each other.

a' 
a 
ber of quotients. Let b' be the convergent immediately preceding b .

or, a(x - b') = b(y - a'). 
Since a and b are prime to each other, b is a divisor of x - b' and a is 
a divisor of y - a'.

7.6. Recurring simple continued fraction. 
A simple continued fraction 
1 
1 
ai + a2+ a3+ · · · 
is said to be a recurring continued fraction if after a certain stage the 
elements recur in the same order. The recurring elements form the cyclic 
part and the non-recurring elements, if they exist, form the acyclic part 
of the continued fraction. 
For example, the continued fraction 
l + 2~ 3~ 4~ 3~ 4~ ••• 
is a recurring continued fraction. Here 1 + ½ is the acyclic part and 3~ ¼ 
is the cycle. 
The cycle is denoted by putting * under the first and the last element 
of the cycle. 
The recurring continued fraction 1 + 2~ 3~ 4~ 3~ 4~ • • • is denoted by 
1 
1 
1 
1 
+2+3-FIT 
* 
*

7. 7. Symmetric continued fraction. 
A finite simple continued fraction is said to be symmetric if the quo-
tients equidistant from the beginning and the end are equal. 
For example, the continued fractions 
1 + i... i... ! 
2 + _L _L _L ! are symmetric continued fractions 
2+ 2+ 1 ' 
3+ 4+ 3+ 2
